Repeated Divorce
   The Muslim is allowed three chances, that is to say, three pronouncements or acts of divorce on three different occasions, provided that each divorce is pronounced during the time when the wife is in the period of purity during which he has had no intercourse with her.
   A husband may divorce his wife once and let the N iddah pass. During the period of S iddah they have the option of reconciliation without the necessity of remarriage. If, however, this waiting period expires without reconciliation, they are now fully divorced. Each of them is free to marry someone else or to remarry each other; should they want to remarry each other, a new marriage contract is required.
   If after the first divorce the husband is reconciled with his wife but later hostility and conflict begin all over again, all efforts at reconciliation and arbitration resulting in failure, he may divorce her a second time in the same manner as described above. In this case, too, he can return to her during the iddah without remarriage, or after the Xiddah has expired through a new marriage contract.
   But it may happen that although he is reconciled with his wife again after the second divorce, he may later divorce her for the third time. This will then be a clear proof that the dislike between the two of them runs very deep and that they are incapable of living together. If this third divorce takes place, it is not permissible for the husband to return to his wife during her iddah, nor may he remarry her after the 'iddah unless she has been m'arried to another man, to live with him as a permanent and true Wife, and he then subsequently divorces her. It is, however, totally prohibited for the other man to marry and divorce her simply in order to make her halal for her first husband.
   Those Muslims who utter three divorce pronouncements at one time or one statetnent are rebels against Allah's law and are deviating from the straight path of Islam. Once the Prophet (pbuh) was informed about a man who had pronounced three divorces at one time. He got up in anger, saying, "Are you delving Allah 's Book even whereas I am still alive among _vou?" A man stood up and said, "0 Messenger of Allah, shall I not kill 
Reconciling Honorably or Separating with Kindness
   When the husband has divorced his wife and the period of Niddah is passing, he h'as two alternatives: either to reconcile with her honorably - that is, to take her back with the intention of living in peace and harmony, and not in order to torment or harm her - or to free her and part with her in kindness by allowing the Niddah to expire without arguments and harsh words, and without any dispute concerning any of their mutual rights.
   It is not lawful for him to take her back just before the N iddah is due to expire in order to torment her by prolonging the waiting period, thus depriving her of the opportunity to marry someone else. This was what was done in the period of Jahiliyyah. Allah (Glorified be He) then prohibited this injury to women in a very decisive manner, using a style of expression which makes the heart quake:
 And when you have divorced women and they have fulfilled the term (of their either retain them honorably or release them honorably; but do not retain them in order to injure them, for this is transgression, and whoever does this has wronged his own soul. And do not take the revelations of Allah in mockery, but remernber Allah's Jhvor upon you and what He has sent down to you of the Book and Wisdom, to instruct you by means of it. And be conscious of Allah, and know that Allah is Ever-Knowing of eventhing.
(Al-Baqarah: 23 1)

l. Narrated by An-Nasa'i,
   A little reflection upon this noble verse of seven phrases, containing warning after warning, reminder after reminder, ought to be sufficient for anyone who has any feeling in his heart or any hearing when it is recited.
The Divorced Woman's Freedom to Remarry
   After the expiration of the divorced woman's Niddah, neither her ex-husband, guardian, nor anyone else can prevent her from marrying anyone she chooses. As long as she and the man who proposes to her follow the procedure required by the Sharüah, no one has the right to interfere. What some men of today do in attempting to prevent their ex-wives from remarrying, intimidating them and their families, is in fact something pertaining to Jahiliyyah; likewise, what some families or guardians of divorced women do to prevent them from returning to their husbands when they want to be reconciled, as indeed ĹPeace is better > (An-Nisa': 128), contradicts the law set by Allah. Allah (Glorified be He) says,
  And when _vou divorce women and they complete their term ( Kiddah), do not prevent them from marrying their (former) husbands if they agree among themselves in an honorable manner, This is to instruct those among you who believe in Allah and the Last Day. That is more virtuous and pure for you; and Allah knows and you do not know.
(Al-Baqarah: 232)
The Woman's Right to Demand Divorce
   The woman who cannot bear to live with her husband has the right to free herself from the marriage bond by returning to her husband the mahr (required marriage dowry) and gifts he has given her, or more or less than that according to their mutual agreement. It is, however, preferable that he should not ask for more than what he has given her. Allah (Glorified be He) says,
And if vou (the judges) fear that the two may not be able to keep to the limits ordained by Allah, there is no blame on either of them if she redeems herself (from the marriage tie by returning all or part of the mahr)...
(Al-Baqarah: 229)
   The wife of Thabit ibn Qays came to the Prophet (pbuh) and said, "O Messenger of Allah, I do not reproach Thabit ibn Qays in respect of character and religion, but I do not want to be guilty of showing anger to him. "( l ) The Prophet (pbuh) asked her about what she had received from him. She replied, "A garden." He asked, "Will you give him back his garden?" "Yes," she said. The Prophet (pbuh) then said to Thabit, "Accept the garden and make one pronouncement of divorce. tf(2)
   It is not permissible for a woman to seek divorce from her husband unless she has met ill treatment from him or unless she has an acceptable reason which requires their separation. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
"If any woman asks her husband for a divorce without some strong reason, the fragrance of Paradise will be forbidden to her.
The Prohibition of Ill Treatment
   It is haram for the husband to torment and mistreat his wife in order to compel her to seek divorce so that she will return to him all or part of the property he has given her. Only if the wife is guilty of clear immorality may her husband demand the return of part of the mahr. In this regard Allah (Glorified be He) says,
... Nor should you treat them with harshness in order that you may take away part of what you have given them, (for you may not take it back) unless they are guilty of open lewdness.
(An-Nisa'.• 19)
   It is also haram for a husband to take back anything from his wife because he hates her and wants to divorce her so he can marry another woman. Almighty Allah says,
ĹBut if you decide to take one wife in the place of another, even if you have given one of them a heap of gold, do not take (back) anything of it; would you take it (back) by slander and a manifest wrong? And could

l. She meant that although Thabit was a good man, she was unable to get along with him and thus might not be able to show him the respect due to him as a husband. (Translator)
2. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and An-Nasati.
3. Narrated by Abu Dawud.
you take it (back), when each of you has been privately with the other, and thev (the wives) have taken a solemn covenant from you?
(An-Nisa': 20-21)
The Prohibition of the Oath of Desertion
   One of the aspects of Islam's concern for the rights of women is that it prohibits a man to show his anger toward his wife by discontinuing sexual relations with her for a period which she cannot bear. If this abandonment of sexual relations is accompanied by an oath of his part, he is given a limit of four months in which he may calm down and revert to her. If he comes to his senses and resumes sexual relations before the expiration of the four months, it is possible that Allah may forgive him for his excess and open the door of repentance to him; however, he must still do the penance prescribed for a broken oath. If, on the other hand, this period expires and he has not returned to her, his wife is divorced from him as a just punishment for his neglect of her rights.
   Some jurists hold that the divorce is automatic at the expiration of four months and that no judgement from a court is needed. Others, however, require that at the end of the period the matter should be referred to the judicial authority, who will then give them the option of reconciliation or divorce.
   Such an oath of abstention from the wife is terminologically known in the Shari Nah as ila'. Concerning it Allah (Glorified be He) says,
For those who take an oath of abstention from their wives, a waiting period of four months (is ordained); if thev return, indeed, Allah is Ever-Forgiving, Ever-Merciful. But if their intention is firm for divorce, then, indeed. Allah is Ever-Hearing, Ever-Knowing.
(Al-Baqarah: 226-227)
   This period of four months has been specified to give the husband an ample time to calm himself and to restore the relationship of his own volition. Moreover, a period of four months is normally regarded as the maximum period a woman can endure separation from her husband. Commentators on the Qur'an narrate the following incident in support of this opinion:
   One night during his caliphate, while Wmar was making a round of Madinah, he heard a woman swearing by Allah that had there been no fear of Him, her cot would be shaking from side to side. s Umar understood what she meant by this when he, upon investigation, found that the woman's husband had gone on a military expedition for a long time. He then asked his daughter Hafsah (the widow of the Prophet (pbuh)), "How long can a woman endure separation from her husband?" She replied, "Four months. Subsequently, the Commander of the Believers decided that he would not send a married man away from his wife for a period exceeding four months.
   

   
6. The Relationship Between Parents and Children
Islam Protects Lineage
   The child is an extension of his father and the bearer of his characteristics. During the father's lifetime he is the joy of his eyes, while after his death he represents a continuation of his existence and an embodiment of his perpetuity. He inherits his features and stature as well as his mental qualities and traits, both the good and the bad, the beautiful as well as the ugly, from his father. The child is a part of his father's heart and a piece of his body.
   Allah (Glory be to Him) has ordained marriage and has forbidden zina so that paternity may be established without doubt or ambiguity and that the child may be referred to his father and the father to his sons and daughters. Through marriage a woman is reserved for one man; it is haram for her to be unfaithful to him or to let anyone else have access to what exclusively belongs to him. Thus, every child born to her in wedlock will be her husband's child, without any need for recognition or public proclamation of the fact by him or a corresponding claim on the part of the mother.
The Prophet of Islam (pbuh) declared,
"The child is attributed to the (one on whose) bed (it is born).
The Prohibition of Denying Paternity
   It is not permissible for the husband to deny his paternity of any child born to his wife as long as they are married to each other. Such a denial would bring the ugliest shame imaginable upon both the wife and the child. He is, therefore, not allowed to take such a step on the basis of a mere suspicion, a sudden notion, or an evil rumor. If, however, on the basis of a

l. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
proof which has been established before him. he is convinced that his wife has betrayed him, the Shari Nah of Islam has no desire to force him to raise a child whom he believes not to be his own or to let the child be his heir, or at the very least - to allow him to suffer from suspicion and doubt the rest of his life.
   A way out of this dilemma, known in Islamic Jurisprudence as li an, is provided by the Sharüah. If a man is convinced or strongly suspects, although without having proof, that his wife has had sexual relation with another man and is carrying his child, he can take the case to a Muslim judge (qadi). The qadi will ask the man and his wife to invoke the curse of Allah on one another in the manner prescribed in Surat an-Nur:
ĹAs for those who accuse their wives but have no witnesses except themselves, the testimony of one of them shall consist of bearing witness by Allah föur times that he is the truthful, and a fifth (time) that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is one of those who lie. And it shall avert the punishment fronz her if she bear witness by Allah four times that he is indeed of thos•e who lie, and a fifth (time) that the wrath ofAllah be upon her if he is among the truthful.
(An-Nur: 6-9)
   After this, they shall be separated permanently, and the child shall be identified by the name of his or her mother.
The Prohibition of Adoption
   Just as it is haram for a man to deny his paternity of a child born to his wife in wedlock, it is likewise haram for him to legally adopt a son of whom he is not the natural father. Like peoples of other societies in the run of history, the Arabs of Jahi/iyyah used to add anyone they wished to their lineage and family through adoption. A man would adopt any boy of his liking making him as his own son, announce that to the public, and the boy would become like a real son to him, sharing the responsibilities and rights of his adopting family and taking its name. The adoption was effective despite the fact that the adopted son might have a known father and come from a known lineage.
   This practice was widespread in Arab society at the advent of Islam. The Prophet (pbuh) had himself adopted Zayd ibn Harithah, who had been captured as a child during one of the raids on his tribe which were common occurrences during the period of Jahiliyyah. Hakim ibn Hizam had bought him for his aunt Khadijah, and after her marriage to the Prophet (pbuh) Khadijah presented Zayd to him. When Zayd's father and uncle knew his place of residence, they came to the Prophet (pbuh) to demand Zayd's return. The Prophet (pbuh) gave Zayd a choice, and he chose to stay with the Prophet (pbuh) in preference to his father and uncle. The Prophet (pbuh) then set him free and adopted him as his son in the presence of others. He was thereafter called Zayd ibn Muhammad and became the first of the freed slaves to accept Islam.
   Now what is the judgement of Islam concerning such a system of adoption? Islam rightly views this sort of adoption as a falsification of the natural order and of reality. Taking a stranger into the family as one of its members and allowing him privacy with women who are not his mahram relatives, nor he theirs, is a deception, for the man ts wife is not his adopted son's mother, nor is his daughter the boy's sister, nor is his sister his aunt, since all of them are non-mahram to him. Moreover, the adopted son acquires a claim on the inheritance of the man and his wife, depriving the rightful, deserving relatives of their inheritance. Such a situation arouses the anger of the real relatives against the intruder who encroaches upon them and usurps their rights, depriving them of the inheritance.( l ) Frequently such anger leads to quarrels and to the breaking of relations among relatives. That is why the Qur'an abolished this jahili system. prohibiting it totally and eradicating all its consequences. Allah (Glorified be He) says,
... Nor has He made your adopted sons your (real) sons; that is simply a saying Q/ your mouths. But Allah speaks the truth, and He guides you 10 the (right way). Call then? by (the names of) their fathers; that is m.ore just in the sight of Allah. But if you do not know their fathers, they are vour brothers-in-faith and your wards...
(Al-Ahzab: 4-5)

l. Since the Islamic Sharüah specifies the share of an individual' propeny to which each near blood relative is entitled, the legal adoption of a child who is not among such relatives, but who, by virtue of adoption. is one of the heirs would naturally create bitterness and hostility among the rightful heirs. (Translator)
   Let us consider the Qur'amc words, "He has not made your adopted sons your (real) sons; that is simply a saying of your mouths This signifies that the declaration of adoption consists of words having no corresponding objective reality. A mere pronouncement does not change realities, alter facts, or make a stranger a relative, or an adopted individual a son. A mere verbal expression or figure of speech cannot make the blood of a man run in the veins of the adopted son, produce feelings of fatherly affection in the man's heart or filial emotions in the heart of the boy, or transfer either the genetic characteristics or physical, mental, or psychological traits.
   Islam abolished all the effects of this system of adoption which relate to inheritance and to prohibition of marriage to the widowed or divorced wife of the adopted son. In matters of inheritance, the Qur'an does not consider any claim except that is based on relationship through blood and marriage:
... But blood relatives are nearer to each other in the ordinance of Allah...
(Al-Anfal: 75)
   With regard to marriage, the Qur'an declares that only the wives of one's real sons, The wives of your sons who are from your (own) (An-Nisa': 23), not the wives of the adopted sons, are permanently forbidden in marriage. Accordingly, it is permissible for a man to marry the divorced wife of his adopted son, since she has been, in actuality, the wife of a "stranger" not related by blood.
A Practical Example of the Abolition of Adoption
   The practice of adopting sons was very rooted in the society of pre-Islamic Arabia, and it was not easy for people to give up. But Allah (Glorified be He) wanted to eradicate it and its effects, not only by words but also by deeds. In order that all doubts concerning the matter might be dispelled, that the believers might feel at ease with respect to marrying the ex-wives of their adopted sons, and, more importantly, that they might know with certainty that the halal is that which is permitted by Allah and that the haram is that which is forbidden by Him alone, Allah (Glorified be He) chose the Prophet (pbuh) himself for this significant task.
   Zayd ibn Harithah, who was known as Zayd ibn Muhammad, had married the Prophet's cousin, Zaynab bint Jahsh. Zayd and Zaynab were not happy together, and Zayd became increasingly dissatisfied with his wife, complaining frequently to the Prophet (pbuh). Although the Prophet (pbuh) knew, through divine revelation, that Zayd would divorce Zaynab and that he himself would marry her afterwards, human weakness occasionally overcame him, and he was afraid of facing the people. Thus, whenever Zayd complained to him about his wife, the Prophet (pbuh) would say to him, "Retain your wife and fear Allah At that point Allah (Glory be to Him) revealed some verses of the Qur'an admonishing the Prophet (pbuh) and at the same time fortifying his will to face society in demolishing the remnants of this ancient system, in this case, the established practice which prohibited a man from marrying the ex-wife of a stranger who had been adopted as a son. Allah (Glorified be He) says,
end when thou didst say to him who had received the favour of Allah and thy favour, Retain thy wife and fear Allah, ' Thou didst hide within thyself what Allah was about to make manifest, fearing the people; but Allah has more right that thou shouldst fear Him. Then, when Zayd had carried out the necessary formality (of divorce) from her, We gave her to thee in marriage so that (in the future) there might be no difficulty for the Believers with respect to (marriage to) the wives of their adopted sons when the latter have carried out the necessary formality (of divorce) from them; and Allah's command must be fulfilled.
(Al-Ahzab: 37)
   The Qur'an goes on to support the Prophet (pbuh) in this action, confirming its lawfulness and removing any stigma attached to it:
  There is no fault in the Prophet in what Allah has made obligatory for him. That was Allah's practice with those old who passed away, and the command of Allah is a decree determined - those who delivered the messages of Allah and feared Him, fearing none but Allah; and Allah suffices in keeping account. Muhammad is not the father of any man among you, but he is the Messenger of Allah and the Seal of the Prophets; and Allah is the Knower of all things.
(Al-Ahzab: 38-40)
Adopting a Child to Rear and to Educate
   As explained above, the type of adoption which has been abolished by Islam is that which makes a boy a member of the family, with all the rights of inheritance, the permissibility of mixing freely with other members of the household, the prohibition of marriage and so on.
   But the word "adoption" is also used in another sense, one which is not prohibited by Islam - that is, when a man brings home an orphan or a foundling to rear, to educate, and to treat as his own child; he protects, feeds, clothes, teaches, and loves the child as his own. However, he does not attribute the child to himself, nor does he give him the rights which the Shari\ah reserves for real children. This is a meritorious act in Allah's religion, and the man who does it will be rewarded by being admitted to Paradise. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
    "I ancl the one who raises an orphan, will be like these two in Paradise, and he pointed with his middle and index fingers with a slight gap between the two.
   A foundling (laqit) is regarded as an orphan (yatim), and it is more reasonable after that the term wayfarer (ibn  one of those who should also be cared for, is applied to him as well.
   If a man has no children of his own, and he wishes to benefit such a child from his wealth, he may give him whatever he wants during his lifetime and may also bequeath to him up to one-third of his inheritance before his death.
Artificial Insemination
   Islam safeguards lineage by prohibiting zina and adoption, thus keeping the family line unambiguously defined without any foreign element entering into it. It likewise prohibits what is known as artificial insemination if the giver of the semen is other than the husband. In such a case, as the well-known Sheikh Shaltut said,
, Ibn as-sabil (Wayfarer) is one of several categories of people mentioned as deserving of charity in vanous Qur'amc verses, notably Al-Baqarah. 176 and At-Tawbah: 60. A foundling or an orphan can also be considered to be belonging in this category and hence as doubly deserving of help and charity. (Translator)
   
   It IS a despicable crime and a major sin, and classified in the same category as -,inu. Zina and artificial insemination by anyone other than the husband both have the same nature and effect; that is, in both cases the tillage which belongs exclusively to the husband is intentionally inseminated by a stranger. Had the form of this crime not been different (from that of zina), such insemination would have been punishable by the same hadd punishment as is prescribed for zina in the divinely revealed
Shari Nah. f '
   There is, however, no doubt that insemination by someone other than the husband is a more serious crime and detestable offense than adoption, for the child born of (such) insemination incorporates in itself the result of adoption - the introduction of an alien elements into the lineage in conjunction with the offense of zina, which is abhorrent both to the divinely revealed laws and to upright human nature. By this action the human being is degraded to the level of an animal, that has no consciousness of the noble bonds (of morality and lineage) which exist among the members of a human society.
A Child's Attributing Himself to a Man Other Than his
Own Father
   Just as Islam prohibits a father to deny his paternity of his own child without a justifiable reason, it likewise forbids the child to claim a lineage other than his own, or to claim as father someone who is not his real father. The Prophet (pbuh) listed this practice among the abominable evils deserving the curse of both the Creator and His creatures. Once speaking from the pulpit, read from some papers where he had written various hadiths. One of the Prophet's statements was the following:
   "The one who claims descent from someone other than his (real) father and the slave who attaches himself to someone other than his (real) master, are cursed by Allah, His angels, and all people. Allah will accept neither repentance nor ransom from such a person on the Day of Resurrection.
And SaX d ibn Abi Waqqas reported that the Prophet (pbuh) said,

l . Shaltut, Al-Fatawa, p. 300
2. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
"If someone claims a man as his father while knowing that he is not, Paradise will be forbidden to him.
Do Not Kill Your Children
   After safeguarding the lineage in this manner, Islam imposed certain mutual rights, which proceed naturally from the parent-child relationship upon children and parents, making certain things haram for them in order to protect these rights.
   The child has a right to live. Neither the father nor the mother have the right to take life of the child, whether a boy or a girl, by killing it or burying it alive, as was done by some Arabs of Jahiliyyah. Allah (Glorified be He) says,
QAnd do not kill your children out offear of poverty; We shall provide for them andfor you. Truly, the killing of them is a great sin.
                                               (Al-Isra': 31)  When the female child who was buried alive is asked for what crime she was killed.
(At-Takwir: 8-9)
   Whatever the motive for this crime may be, whether economic, such as fear of poverty and lack of provision, or non-economic, such as fear of disgrace in the case of a daughter, Islam absolutely prohibits this savage act which is nothing but premeditated murder and oppression against a feeble, helpless human being. That is why, when the Prophet (pbuh) was asked, "What is the greatest sin?" he replied, "To ascribe divinity to someone other than Allah, when He is One Who created you". "What is next?" he was asked. "To kill your child out offear that it will share yourfood, " he replied.(2 )
        The Prophet (pbuh) took an oath of allegiance from both men and women at the time of their accepting Islam. This oath of allegiance included  the condition that they would not kill their children and would consider it an absolutely prohibited crime:
... That they will not steal nor commit zina nor kill their children
(Al-Mumtahanah: 12)

l. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and Muslim. 2. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
   It is the right of a child in relation to his parents that they should give it a good name, not one which will cause it disturbance when it grows older. It is haram to give a name which denotes that it is a worshiper of someone other than Allah, as for example 'Abd an-Nabi (servant - or worshiper - of the Prophet), %Abd al-Masih (servant - or worshiper - of Christ), and the like.
   A child has a right to sustenance, education, and proper care. The parents are not permitted to neglect the child's needs nor to abuse them. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
"Each one of you is a caretaker (ra X i) and is responsible for those under his care.

Wasting the sustenance of his dependants is sufficient sin for a man.
"Allah will ask every caretaker (röi) about what He entrusted him to take care of whether he has done the care-taking well or otherwise, and (every) man will be asked concerning the people of his household.
Equal Treatment of Children
   It is obligatory for a father to treat all his children equally, especially in the matter of giving gifts. Accordingly, he is prohibited to bestow on some of his children more favors than on others without any necessity or valid reason, since this will produce jealousy and may even arouse enmity and hatred among them. This applies equally to the mother. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
     "Do justice among your sons, repeating it three times.(4)
   The story behind this hadith is that the wife of Bashir ibn Söd al-Ansari requested her husband to give a gift of a garden or a slave to her son, An-Nux man ibn Bashir. She asked Bashir to go to the Prophet (pbuh) and request him to be a witness. Bashir went to him and said, "The daughter of such and such - meaning his wife - has asked me to give a slave to her son.
"Does he have brothers?" the Prophet (pbuh) asked. "Yes," he replied. "Did

Observing the Limits of Allah Regarding Inheritance
   It is haram for a father to deprive his children of inheritance, as for example, to deprive the females or the children of a wife who is not a favorite to him. Likewise, it is haram for one relative to deprive another eligible relative of his inheritance by means of a trick. It is Allah (Glory be to Him) Himself, Who, out of His knowledge, wisdom, and justice, has established the distribution of inheritance in order to give each eligible person his or her share, and He has commanded mankind to remain within the limits of His legislation; hence, anyone who deviates from His system in the distribution of shares offends his Lord.
   Allah (Glorified be He) has mentioned matters of inheritance in three verses of the Qur'an. At the end of the first verse He says,
 ... Your fathers or your sons: you do not know which of them is nearer to you in benefit. This is an obligation ordained by Allah; indeed, Allah
is Knower, Wise.
(An-Nisat : 11)

... Fire, to abide therein forever, and he shall have a humiliating punishment.
(An-Nisa': 14)
Disobedience to Parents: A Major Sin
   It is the right of parents that their children should treat them with kindness, obedience, and honor. Devotion to parents is a natural instinct which must be strengthened by deliberate actions. The rights of the mother are stressed more because of her suffering during pregnancy and childbirth, her suckling of the child, and her role in rearing it. Allah (Glorified be He) says,
'And We have enjoined on man kindness to his parents. His mother carries him in pain and she gives birth to him in pain, and (the period) of carrying him and weaning him is thirty months... 
	(Al-Ahqaf: 15)	
   Once, a man came to the Prophet (pbuh) and asked, "Who is most deserving of my good companionship?" "Your mother, " replied the Prophet
   
(pbuh). "Who is next?" asked the man. 'Your mother, replied the Prophet
(pbuh). "Who is next?" asked the man. Your mother, replied the Prophet
(pbuh). "Who is next?" asked the man. 'Your father, replied the Prophet

   The Prophet (pbuh) declared disobedience to parents to be a major sin, second only to ascribing partners to Allah, as has been stated in the Qur'an. Al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated that he (pbuh) once said, "Shall I not inform you about the three major sins?" Those who were present replied, "Yes, O Messenger of Allah." He said, "Associating partners with Allah and disobedience to parents, " and sitting up from the reclining position, he continued, "and telling lies and false testimony; beware of it".
He is also reported to have said,
"Three persons shall not enter Paradise: the one who is disobedient to his parents, the pimp, and the woman who imitates men.
and,
"Allah defers (the punishment of) all sins to the Day of Resurrection excepting disobedience to parents, for which Allah punishes the sinner in this life before his death.
   Moreover, Islam emphasizes treating parents kindly, especially when they grow old. As their strength fails, they require more attention and care, more consideration of them, and even more sensitive feelings. Concerning this, the Qur'an says,
Your Lord has decreed that you worship none but Him and that you be kind to parents. If one or both of them attain old age with you, do not say a word of annoyance( 4) to them nor repulse them, but speak to them in gracious words and in mercy lower to them the wing of humility and say, 'My Lord, bestow Thy mercy on thenl, as they cherished me when I was little'.
(Al-Isra': 23-24)

Causing One's Parents to Be Insulted: A Major Sin
   In addition to the foregoing, the Prophet (pbuh) not only prohibited causing one's parents to be insulted but also declared it to be a major sin. He once said,
"Among the major sin is a man's cursing his parents
The people who were present wondered how a sane and believing individual could curse his own parents, and they inquired, "How is it possible for a man to curse his own parents?" The Prophet (pbuh) replied,
'He insults another man's father, and then the other insults his father, and he insults the other's mother, and the other returns the insult to his mother. "(l )
So what would be the position of one who insults his parents directly?
The Parents' Consent for Jihad
   Pleasing one's parents is considered so important in Islam that the son is forbidden to volunteer for jihad without his parent's permission, in spite of the fact that fighting in the cause of Allah (jihadfi sabil Allah) has such great merit in Islam that the merit of a person who spends his nights in prayer and his days in fasting fall short of it.
Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-%As reported,
   "A man came to the Prophet (pbuh) and asked his permission to go for jihad. The Prophet (pbuh) asked, 'Are your parents living?' t Yes,' he replied. The Prophet (pbuh) then said, 'Then strive in their service.
The Prophet (pbuh) meant that he should make the field of jihad his taking care of his parents.

Non-Muslim Parents
   It is one of the beauties of Islam that, with respect to the treatment of parents, it forbids the Muslim to be disrespectful to them even if they should be non-Muslims who are fanatical to the point of arguing with him and putting pressure on him to renounce Islam.
Allah (Glorified be He) says,
  Be grateful to Me and to the parents; to Me is (the final) goal. But if they strive to compel thee to associate with Me that of which thou hast no knowledge, do not obey them; hut keep company with them in this life

l. Narrated by Muslim.

in a Kind lilanncr and follow the way thn€e who turn to me. Then to Me will be your return and I will infornt you (of the meaning of) all that vou did. 
(Luqman: 14-15)
   In these two verses the Muslim is commanded not to obey his parents in what they try to tell him to do in this regard, since there cannot be obedience to a creature in sin against the Creator - and what sin could be greater than associating partners with Allah? At the same time, he is commanded to treat them honorably in this world, unaffected by their stand against his faith, and to follow the path of those righteous Believers who turn to Allah and to leave the judgement between himself and his parents to the Judge of most just of judges, on a Day when the parents will not be able to benefit the child nor the child the parent. Indeed, such tolerant and beneficent teachings are not to be found in any other religion.

1 . Beliefs and Customs
   Faith (iman) is the foundation of the Islamic society, and tawhid (the belief in the Oneness of Allah) is the essence of this faith and the very core of Islam. The safeguarding of this iman and of this pure tawhid is the primary objective of all the Islamic teachings and legislations. In order to keep the Muslim society purified of all traces of shirk and remnants of error, a continuous war must be waged against all belief-systems which originate in man's ignorance of the divine guidance and in the errors of idol worship.
Respect for Allah's Laws in the Universe
   One of the fundamental beliefs which Islam inculcates in the soul of Muslims is that this vast universe does not run itself without any control and guidance, nor does it follow the misguided, blind, conflicting, and contradictory desires of men or of any other creatures residing in it. The Qur'an says,
{encl if truth ever followed their liking, the heavens and the earth, and whosoever is therein, would have been in corruption...
(Al-Mu'minun: 71)
   Quite to the contrary, the universe is bound by permanent laws, as the Qur'an states,
... Thou wilt not find any changes in the sunnah (practice or rule) of Allah, nor wilt thoufind in the sunnah ofAllah any turning aside.
(Fatir: 43)
   Muslims have learned from the Book of their Lord and the practice of their Prophet (pbuh) to respect these laws of the universe, to understand and to use the causes and relationships which Allah has established among things, and to reject the alleged esoteric causes propagated by priests, charlatans, and impostors.

The War Against Superstitions and Myths
   A class of deceivers known as soothsayers or diviners existed in Arab society during the Prophet's time; they pretended to know the events of the past and future through their contact with the jinn or through other secret sources. The Prophet (pbuh) then declared war on this deception, which had no basis in knowledge, divine guidance, or a revealed scripture. He recited to them what Allah had revealed to him:
Say: No one in the heavens and the earth knows the Unseen except Allah.•• 
(An-Naml: 65)
   Accordingly, the Unseen is known neither to the angels, the jinn nor human beings. Acting on the command of this Lord, the Prophet (pbuh) proclaimed,
 If I had knowledge of the Unseen, I should have had abundance of good and no evil should have touched me. Truly, I am but a warner and a bringer of good tidings to th.ose who have faith.
(Al-Rraf: 188)
   Concerning the jinn who labored for Prophet Sulayman (Solomon), Allah (Glorified be He) says,
It became clear to the jinn that if they had known the Unseen, they would not have continued in the hunqiliating punishment (of their task). 
(Saba': 14)
   Thus, anyone who claims to know what pertains to the Unseen utters a falsehood against Allah and the truth, deceiving people.
   Once a delegation came to the Prophet (pbuh) and supposing him to be one of those who claimed to have knowledge of the Unseen, they concealed something in their hands, asking the Prophet (pbuh) to tell them what it was. The Prophet (pbuh) said to them in plain words,
'7 am not a diviner. The diviner, (what pertains to) the divination, and t/ae soothsavers will all be in the Fire. "
236
Believing in Those Who Foretell the Future Constitutes KL4fr
   Islam's campaign is not only confined to the soothsayers and diviners but includes all those who go to them, ask for their help, and believe in their superstitions and errors. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
'The Prayer of one who goes to a soothsayer, asks him for something and believes in what he says will not be acceptedforforty days. "( l )
He also said,
"Whoever goes to a soothsayer and believes in what he says has denied what vvus revealed to Muhammad.
This is because what was revealed to Muhammad (pbuh) asserts that the knowledge of the Unseen belongs to Allah alone and that Muhammad (pbuh) has no knowledge of it, much less anyone else:
 Say: I do not tell you that the treasures of Allah are with me or that I know the Unseen, nor do I tell .you that I am an angel; I follow only what is revealed to me...
(Al-Arfam: 50)
   If, after being aware of this clear and explicit statement of the Qur'an, a Muslim believes that some people can foretell the future and know the secrets of the Unseen, he has indeed denied what was revealed to the Messenger of Allah (pbuh).
Divination with Arrows
   For the reason mentioned above, divination with arrows is prohibited by Islam. The Arabs of Jahiliyyah used three arrows for divination; on one arrow was written, "My lord commanded me," on another, "My lord forbade me," and the third was left blank. If they planned to go on a journey, to marry, to carry out a raid, etc., they would go to the temple where these arrows were kept. One arrow would be selected randomly, If they selected the "commanding" arrow they would proceed with their plan; if they selected the "forbidding" arrow they would not proceed with it; while if the

l. Reported by Muslim.
2. Narrated by Al-Bazzar with a good and well-established chain of transmitters.

   
blank arrow was drawn they would replace it and repeat the process until they received a clear indication.
   The practices in our society of making decisions on the basis of what is observed in sand, seashells, tea leaves, cards, palms, of opening a book at random, and the like are similar to this  Islam has prohibited all such practices and considers them sinful. After mentioning the prohibited foods, Allah (Glory be to Him) says,
... And (also forbidden) is predicting the future by means of divining arrows, for that is im.piety...
(Al-Malidah: 3)
And the Prophet (pbuh) said,
"He who consults with soothsayers or divining arrows, or returns from a journey because of an ill omen, shall not attain the high rank (in Paradise).
Magic
   In like manner, Islam condemns magic and those who practice it. Concerning those who learn magic the Qur'an says,
... They learned (onlv) what harmed them and what did not benefit them
(Al-Baqarah: 103)
   The Prophet (pbuh) counted the practice of magic among those major deadly sins which destroy nations before destroying individuals and which degrade those who practice them in this world prior to the Hereafter, he said, "Avoid the seven destructive things. " The listeners asked, "O Messenger of Allah, what are they?" He said,
"Associating partners with Allah (shirk), magic, taking a life which
Allah has made sacred except in the course ofjustice, devouring riba,

The Messenger of Allah (pbuh) disowned such persons, saying,

Charms and Amulets
   In the same category is the hanging of charms, seashells and the like in the belief that they will bring about the cure of a disease or act as a protection from it. There are still some people in the present century who hang a horseshoe on the door. Moreover, we still find today charlatans in various countries who exploit the ignorance of simple people by writing amulets and charms for them, drawing lines and talismans and reciting strange incantations, with the claim that these practices will protect the bearer from the aggression of evil spirits, the influence of demons, the evil eye, envy, and so on.
   As far as the prevention and treatment of disease are concerned, Islam has prescribed measures which are well known, condemning those who turn away from them to the deceitful methods of swindlers. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
    Seek the remedy, for He Who created illness also created its cure. He also said,
"There is a remedy in three things: a drink of honey, bleeding by a copper, and cauterization by fire.
   In our time these three of cures include, by analogy and extension, all medicines which are taken by mouth, surgical intervention, and therapies utilizing heat or electricity.

l. Reported by Ibn Hibban in his Sahih. 2. Reported by Ahmad.
3. Reported by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
   
   As for wearing beads, seashells, charms and amulets, or reciting certain incantations to treat or prevent illness, such practices are sheer ignorance and error and contrary to the laws of Allah (Glorified be He), and constitute a denial of tawhid.
   Uqbah ibn reported that he came to the Prophet (pbuh) in a group of ten persons. The Prophet (pbuh) accepted the oath of allegiance from nine of thenm, withholding hirnself fronl the tenth. "What about hill)?" they asked. "There is an atnulet on his arm, " the Prophet (pbuh) replied. The man tore off the amulet and the Prophet (pbuh) then accepted his oath and said, "The one who wears (it) is a polytheist.
The Prophet (pbuh) also said,
"Mav Allah not fulfill the hopes of the one vvho wears a charm; mav Allah not protect the one who hangs seashells.
   Imran ibn Husayn reported that the Prophet (pbuh) saw a man wearing a brass bracelet in his arm and he said to him, "Woe to you, what is this?" He replied, "To protect me from weakness." The Prophet (pbuh) said,
"Indeed, this only increases your weakness. Throw it away, for if you die wearing it, you will never attain success (in the Hereafter). "(3)
   These teachings of the Prophet (pbuh) penetrated the minds of his Companions, and they rejected such erroneous and false practices, neither accepting nor believing in them. ibn Hamzah reported, "I visited Abdullah ibn Hakim who had a fever. I said, 'Why do you not wear a charm'?' He replied, 'I seek refuge in Allah from that.' In another version he said, "Death is preferable to that." The Messenger of Allah (pbuh) said,
'Whoever wears a charm will be left to rely on it.
   Abdullah ibn Mae ud once saw his wife wearing a knotted thread around her neck. He pulled at and broke it, saying, "The family of Abdullah is free of associating anything with Allah for which He has sent no authority." Then he said, "I heard the Messenger of Allah (pbuh) say,

'Incantations, amulets, and spells are (signs of) shirk.
   Thereupon, someone said to him, "Abu ar-Rahman (as he was commonly called), we know what incantations and amulets are, but what is spells tawlah?" He said, "Something which women employ to make their husbands love Accordingly, tawlah denotes a kind of magical practice.
   Scholars say that if incantations are in a foreign language so that one does not know what is being said, they are prohibited out of fear of their being mixed with unbelief and magic. However, if what is being said can be understood and there is mention of Allah in it, it is commendable because it is then a supplication to Allah and is not meant to be a cure or a medicine. The incantations of Jahiliyyah were intermixed with magical formulae, polytheistic phrases, and nonsensical utterances.
   It is narrated that v Abdullah ibn Mae ud forbade his wife to utter such jahili incantations. She said to him, "I went out one day and saw such and such person. One of my eyes then began to water (meaning that it was the effect of his evil eye and envy). But when I recited an incantation it stopped watering, and when I left off reciting it, the eye started watering again." Ibn Mashid said, "That is Satan. When you obey him he leaves you alone, but when you disobey him he stabs your eye with his finger. But if you do as the Prophet (pbuh) did, it will be better for you and will most probably cure your eye. Bathe your eye with water and say,
'Remove the hurt, O Lord of mankind. Heal me; You are the Healer. There is no cure except Your cure which leaves no disease behind.
Omens
   Drawing evil omens from certain articles, places, times, individuals, and the like was, and still is a current superstition. In antiquity, the people of the Prophet Salih (peace be upon him) said to him,
We augur an evil omen ofthee and those with thee...
(An-Naml: 47)

l. Reported by Ibn Hibban in his Sahih,
2. Reported by Ibn Majah.

And whenever a calamity struck them, Pharaoh and his people
... ascribed it to evil omens connected with Musa and those with hint...
(Al-Rraf: 31)
Many times, when Allah (Glorified be He) tried the unbelievers by sending a calamity, they would say to the Messenger of Allah (pbuh),
... Indeed, vv•e augur an evil omen from you...
(Yasin: 18)
The reply of the Messengers was,
Q. Your auguring of evil omens is with yourselves... 
(Yasin: 19)
This means, "The cause of your evil omens is in your own attitude, stemming from your unbelief, stubbornness, and arrogance in regard to Allah and His Messengers."
   The Arabs of Jahiliyyah had a long history of such practices associated with a variety of beliefs which persisted until the coming of Islam, which abolished all such notions and brought the people back to the way of sound reason. The Prophet (pbuh) classified the auguring of evil omens with divination and magic in his saying,
"He is not of us who seeks for evil omens or for whom evil omens are sought, who divines or for whom divination is made, who practices magic orfor whom magic is practiced.
The Prophet (pbuh) also said,
"Augury from drawing lines in the sand, from the flight of birds, and from throwing stones pertains to shirk.
   The auguring of omens has no basis in science or in reality, but is weakness of the mind and a sdperstition. How can a sane human being believe that a certain person or place, the cry of a bird, the flick of an eyelid, or the hearing of a certain word can foretell something evil? Even if there is

l. Reported by At-Tirmidhi.
2. Reported by Abu Dawud
243
sonle weakness in human nature which is conductive to the seeking of omens from certain things, one should not surrender to this weakness, especially when a decision is to be made or an action is to be taken. It is stated in a hadith that
"No one is free of three things: suspicion, auguring evil omens, and envy. Thus, if you. have a suspicion, do not pursue it; if you augur an evil onzen, do not turn back; and if vou are envious, do not transgress.
   In this way these three things will remain mere thoughts which cross the mind without affecting the actual behavior, and Allah (Glorified be He) will forgive them. Ibn Masx ud reported the Prophet (pbuh) as saying three times,
"Auguring evil omens is shirk (polytheism). "
   Ibn Maeud added, "None of us fails to be affected by this, but Allah removes such influences through our trust in Him, meaning that although there is no one among us who is not affected by this weakness at one time or another, this weakness is removed from the heart of the person who turns to Allah, trusting in Him and not letting such ideas obsess him.
The War Against Jahili Customs
   On the one hand Islam launched an attack on jahili beliefs and superstitions which were a threat to reason, morals, and manners, and on the other, on jahili customs, which were the product of chauvinism: boastfulness, pride, and the glorification of tribes.
No Chauvinism in Islam
   Islam's first step in this direction was to reduce every kind of group chauvinism to dust, forbidding the Muslim to revive any of the disputes of such chauvinism or to allure others to it. The Prophet (pbuh) declared himself free of responsibility for anyone who practices it, saying,
"He who calls others to group c.hauvinism does not belong to us; he who fights for the sake of group chauvinism does not belong to us; and he who dies upholding group chauvinism does not belong to us.

i. Narrated by At-Tabarani. 2. Narrated by Abu Dawud.
3. Narrated by Abu Dawud.

   
   There is no special distinction for a certain color of skin, a particular race of mankind, or a special region of the earth. The Muslim is forbidden to be a partisan of one race against another, one people against another, or one country against another. It is not permissible for a believer in Allah and the Last Day to support his people only because he is related to them no matter whether they are right or wrong, just or unjust.
   Wah llah ibn al-Asqö reported, "I asked, 'O Messenger of Allah, what is chauvinism?' and he replied, That you should help your people in wrongdoing.
And Allah (Glorified be He) says,
 O vou who believe, be steadfast in justice, as witnesses for Allah, even though it be against yourselves or parents or kindred...
(An-Nisat : 135)
 And do not let hatred of (other) people cause you to deviate from justice...
(Al-Ma'idah: 8)
   "Help your brother, whether he is the offender or the offended," was a well-known proverb in pre-Islamic Jahiliyyah which people used to take literally. The Prophet (pbuh) changed its meaning in a subtle fashion. After the faith was firmly established in the hearts of his Companions, he once repeated this proverb to them. They were shocked and said, "O Messenger of Allah, we know how to help the offended, but how can we help the offender?" He replied, "Stop him from wrongdoing; that is helping him.
   We know from these statements that a call toward nationalism or racism is a call of Jahiliyyah, and Islam, its Prophet (pbuh), and its Book have totally rejected it. Islam does not recognize any loyalty other than to its belief, any relationship other than that of its brotherhood, or any differentiation among human beings other than on the basis of belief and unbelief. Even though he may be a fellow countryman, a relative, or one's own blood brother, the unbeliever who shows hostility to Islam is an enemy to the Muslim.

l. Narrated by Abu Dawud.
2. Narrated by Al-Bukhari.

Allah (Glorified be He) says,
  Thou wilt not find any people who believe in Allah and the Last Day having affection for the ones who contravene Allah and His Messenger, even if they are their fathers or their sons or their brothers or their kindred...
(Al-Mujadalah: 22)
 O you who believe, do not take your fathers or your brothers as friends if they love unbelief abovejhith...

Boasting about One's Lineage and Color
   Al-Bukhari narrated that Abu Dharr and Bilal the Abyssinian, both of whom were among the earliest Muslims, once quarreled and insulted each other. Carried away by his anger, Abu Dharr said to Bilal, "You are son of a black woman!" Bil'al complained about this to the Prophet (pbuh), who turned to Abu Dharr, saying,
"Are your taunting him about his mother? There is still some influence of Jahiliyyah in you.
Abu Dharr reported that the Prophet (pbuh) said to him,
"Look! You are no better than a white or black man unless you excel him in the fear of Allah. "(2 )
The Prophet (pbuh) also said,
"You are all children of Adam, and Adam was created of dust.
   Thus Islam makes it haram for the Muslim to boast about his genealogy and kinship, mentioning his forefathers and saying, "I am the son of such and such," or "I am white and you are black, I am an Arab and you are a non-Arab." What is the value of kinship and genealogies when all people come from one single origin? And even supposing that genealogy had a value, how does it add to the credit or debit of a person to have been born to this or that father? The Prophet (pbuh) said,

l. Reported by Al-Bukhari.
2. Reported by Al-Bukhari.
3. Reported by Ahmad.

"These genealogies of yours are not a reason to revile anyone. You are all children of Adam. No one has superiority over another except in religion and taqwa (the fear of Allah).
"Mankind is descended from Adam and Eve.... On the Day of Resurrection Allah will not ask you about your kinship and genealogies. The most honorable among you in the sight of Allah is the one who is the most God-fraring.
   The Prophet (pbuh) launched a fierce attack against those who boast about their fathers and grandfathers, saying,
"Let people cease to boast about their ancestors who have died, who are merely fuel in hell, or they will certainly be of less account than the beetle which rolls dung with its nose. Allah has removed from you the pride of Jahilivyah and its boasting about ancestors. One is either a God-fearing believer or a wicked sinner. All people are children of Adam, and Adam was created of dust. 
   People who boast about their remote ancestors among the Pharaohs or the Choesroes (the rulers of ancient Persia) and the like should take note of this hadith. As the Messenger of Allah (pbuh) stated, these ancestors of theirs, whether Arab or non-Arab, or of pre-Islamic Jahiliyyah, are nothing but the fuel of Hell.
   During the Farewell Pilgrimage, when thousands of Muslims gathered in the sacred place, during the sacred month, the Prophet (pbuh) delivered his farewell sermon, emphasizing the basic principles:
"0 people, your Lord is One. Beware that there is no superiority of an Arab over a non-Arab or of a non-Arab over an Arab, nor of a white over a black or of a black over a white, except through fear of Allah (taqwa). Verily, the most honorable among you in the sight of Allah is the one 'vvho has most taqwa.

Mourning for the Dead
   Among the customs of Jahiliyyah which were denounced by Islam was the practice of wailing, lamenting, and showing excessive grief for the dead.
   Islam's teaching concerning death is that it is not the annihilation of an individual, causing him to become non-existent, but that it is a journey from one world to another and that no amount of mourning will bring the dead back to life or change the decree of Allah (Glory be to Him). The believer should receive death, as he receives any other calamity which may befall him, with patience and dignity, repeating the Qur'anic words:
... To Allah we belong and to Him do we return.
(Al-Baqarah: 156)
   The pre-Islamic manner of mourning for the dead is strictly forbidden to the Muslim. The Prophet (pbuh) declared,
"He who slaps his cheeks, tears his clothes and cries out in the manner of Jahi/iyyah is not of us.
   The Muslim is not permitted to wear a mourning band, discard his adornment, or change his usual attire to express his sorrow and grief.(2) However, a wife must observe a mourning period of four months and ten days for her deceased husband in loyalty to the sacred ties of marriage; in Islam this period is considered an extension of her previous marriage and she is not allowed to receive any new proposals of marriage during this period. Thus, she is required to refrain from adorning herself during that time in order to keep the thought of remarriage out of her own mind and that of her potential suitors. However, if the deceased is someone other than her husband, for example, her father, brother or son, it is haram for her to mourn for more than three days. Al-Bukhari narrated concerning Umm Habibah and Zaynab bint Jahsh, both of whom were wives of the Prophet (pbuh), that at the time of the deaths of Umm Habibah's father, Abu Sufyan ibn Harb, and Zaynab's brother, each of them perfumed herself, saying "By Allah, I am not in need of perfume, but I heard Allah's Messenger (pbuh) say,

   The period of mourning for the deceased husband is obligatory and should not be violated. A woman came to the Prophet (pbuh) and said, "My daughter's husband has died, and her eye is infected. May she use kohl The Prophet (pbuh) said, "No, " and repeated it twice or thrice.( 3 ) This demonstrates that adorning or beautifying herself during the prescribed period of mourning is prohibited to the widow. As grief and the expression of it are natural, she may mourn and weep but without wailing and shouting. Upon the death of Khalid ibn al-Walid, x Umar heard some women weeping for his death. Some people wanted to stop them from it but Wmar said, "Let them weep for Abu Sulayman (the name by which Khalid was called), as long as they do not throw dust on their heads or start crying out."

2. Dealings and Transactions
   Allah (Glory be to Him) created human beings in a state of dependence upon one another. Each individual does not own all the things he needs; one person has something which he can spare while at the same time he may need something which others have and which they can spare. Allah has directed people toward exchanging goods and utilities through buying and selling because such transactions make social and economic life function smoothly and encourage people to be productive.
   Various types of transactions and exchanges of property were current among the Arabs at the dawn of the Prophet's mission. He approved and confirmed such types of transactions which did not conflict with the principles of the Shari Nah and disapproved and prohibited those business practices which were against the purposes and aims of the Shari Nah. The prohibitions were due to specific reasons, as, for example, trading in haram goods, transactions involving fraud or exorbitant profits, or injustice to one of the contracting parties.
The Prohibition of Selling Haram Goods
   Trading in goods which are normally used for committing sin is haram. Examples of such things are pork, intoxicants, and other prohibited kinds of food in general, as well as idols, crosses, statues, and the like. Permitting the sale or trade of such articles implies promoting and encouraging them among people to do what is haram, while prohibiting their sale implies suppressing and ignoring them, thereby preventing people from coming into contact with them. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
    "Surely, Allah and His Messenger have prohibited the sale of intoxicants, the flesh of dead animals, swine, and idols, and also

l. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
"When Allah prohibits something, He prohibits (giving and receiving) the price of it as well. l )
The Prohibition of a Sale Involving Uncertainty
   The Prophet (pbuh) forbade any kind of transaction which could lead to a quarrel or litigation due to some uncertainty( 2 ) or which involved an unspecific quantity to be exchanged or delivered. This includes the sort of transaction in which there is no guarantee that the seller can deliver the goods for which he receives payment. Accordingly, the Prophet (pbuh) forbade selling what is in a stallion's or male camcl t s loins, fish in the water, or birds in the air, or the offspring of a camel still in the female t s womb, since there is an element of uncertainty as to the outcome in all such transactions.
   The Prophet (pbuh) observed that people sold unripened fruits which were still in the fields or orchards; if the crop were destroyed by blight or some natural calamity, the buyer and seller would quarrel over who was to bear the loss. Hence, the Prophet (pbuh) prohibited the sale of fruit until they were clearly in good  unless they were to be picked on the spot. Similarly, he forbade selling ears of corn until they were white and safe from blight.( 4 ) and said,
"If Allah withholds the fruit, how can any oj you accept his brother's ntonev as a lawful gain
   However, not every sale involving what is unknown or uncertain is prohibited; for example, a person may buy a house without knowing the condition of its foundation or what is inside the walls. What is prohibited is selling something about which there is an obvious element of uncertainty which may lead to dispute and conflict, or may result in the unjust appropriation of other people's money. Again, If the risk of uncertainty is little - and this is determined by experience and custom - the sale is not

l. Narrated by Ahmad and Abu Dawud.
2. See the chapter on the prohibition of gharar (transactions involving uncertainty) in Sahih Muslim and other books of Hadith.
3. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
4. Narrated by Muslim.
5. Narrated by Al-Bukhari and others.
prohibited. For example, one may sell root vegetables such as carrots. onions, and radishes while they are still in the ground, or fields of cucumbers, watermelons and the like. In the opinion of Imam Malik, all such sales of needed items in which the margin of risk is bearable are
permissible.( l )
Price Manipulation
   In Islam the market is to be free and permitted to respond to the natural laws of supply and demand. Thus, when the prices became high in the Prophet's time and people asked him to fix prices for them, he replied,
"Allah is the One Who fixes prices, Who withholds, Who gives lavishly, and Who provides, and I hope that when I meet Him none of you will have a claim against me for any injustice with regard to blood or property. "(2)
   With these words the Prophet of Islam (pbuh) declared that unnecessary interference in the freedom of individuals is injustice and that one should meet Allah free of blame for such a thing. If, however, any artificial forces, such as h0'arding and manipulation of prices by certain merchants, interfere in the free market, public interest takes precedence over the freedom of such individuals. In such a situation price control becomes permissible in order to meet the needs of the society and to protect it from greedy opportunists by thwarting their schemes, for the above hadith does not mean that price control is prohibited regardless of the circumstances, even if it removes harm and prevents obvious injustice. Researchers among scholars have concluded that, depending on the nature of the circumstances, price control may at times be unjust and prohibited, and at other times may be just and permissible.
   If price control compels people to sell their goods at a price which is not acceptable to them or denies them the reasonable profit permitted by Allah,

l. In Al-Qawöid an-Nuranivyah, p. 1 18, Ibn Taymiyah said, "The principles laid down by Imam Malik concerning sales are superior to those of others, because he took them from Sa•id ibn al-Musayyab, who is the best authority on the juristic rulings regarding sales." Imam Ahmad ibn
Hanbars opinion is close to that of Malik.
	2. 	Ahmad, Abu Dawud, At-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah9 Ad-Darimi, and Abu Ya' la.
   
it is haram. If, on the other hand, price control establishes equity among people, for example, by forcing sellers to accept a price equal to that commanded by other comparable commodities and restraining them from taking more than this, it is allowed - indeed necessary.
   The hadith cited above relates to the first type of situation. Accordingly, if merchants are selling a commodity in the customary fashion without any wrong-doing on their part and the price subsequently rises due to the scarcity of the commodity or due to an increase in population (indicating the operation of the law of supply and demand), this circumstance is from Allah, in which case to force them to sell the commodity at a fixed price would be•unjust compulsion.
   In relation to the second type of situation, should the dealers in a commodity refuse to sell it, despite the fact that people are in need of it, unless they secure a price higher than its known value, they must be compelled to sell it at a price equal to the price of an equivalent commodity. Price control here means nothing more than establishing comparable prices for equivalent commodities and it is therefore in conformity with the standard of justice demanded by Allah (Glorified be
Hoarding Is Condemned
   Freedom for individual and natural competition in the marketplace is guaranteed by Islam. Nevertheless, Islam severely condemns those who, driven by ambition and greed, accumulate wealth at the expense of others and become rich by manipulating the prices of food and other necessities. This is why the Prophet (pbuh) denounced hoarders in very strong words, saying,
"If anyone withholds grain for forty days out of the desire for a high price, Allah will renounce him. 
He also said,
"If anyone withholds goods until the price rises, he is a sinner.

l. Refer to Risalat al-Hisbah by Ibn Taymiyah, as well as to At-Turuq al-Hukmiyyah by Ibn al-Qayyim, p. 214 ff.
2. Ahmad, Al-Hakim, ibn Abi Shaybah, and Al-Bazzar.
3. by Muslim.
   And the term "sinner" here is not to be taken lightly. It is the same epithet which Allah (Glorified be He) applied to some of the great tyrants in history, for example:
... Assuredly Pharaoh and Haman and their hosts were sinners.
(Al-Qasas: 8)
The Prophet (pbuh) also said,
    "The man who hoards goods is evil. If prices fall he is grieved and if they rise he is happy, thereby exposing the selfish and greedy mentality of hoarders.
Again, he said,
"He who brings goods to the market is blessed with bounty, but he who withholds them is cursed.
   There are two ways of making a profit in a business. One is to withhold the commodity from the market until it becomes scarce and those who need it are unable to find it; then, compelled by their need, they come to the hoarder and pay him the price he demands, although it may be unreasonably high. The other way is to put the commodity on the market, sell it for a reasonable profit, buy more goods and sell them in like manner, and so on. Since this latter practice serves the public interest, a merchant who practices it is both blessed by Allah and well-provided for, as the foregoing hadith stated.
   A very important hadith concerning hoarding and manipulating prices was reported by Ma&qal ibn Yasar, a Companion of the Prophet (pbuh). The Umayyad governor, N Ubaydullah ibn Ziyad, came to visit Max qal when he was bedridden due to a grave illness. After inquiring about his condition, Ubaydullah asked him, 'Do you know of any instance of my having wrongfully shed someone's blood?" Möqal replied that he did not. "Do you know of any instance," X Ubaydullah continued, "in which I interfered with the prices of the Muslims' goods?" Max qal again replied that he did not know. Then MaÄal asked the people to help him to sit up, which they did.

l. Ar-Razi mentioned this hadith in his Jami
2. 	Ibn Majah and Al-Hakim.
He then said, 'Listen, O Wbaydullah, and I will tell you something which I heard from the Messenger of Allah (pbuh). I heard the Messenger of Allah (pbuh) say,
'Whoever interj?res with the prices of the Muslims' goods in order to raise them deserves that Allah should make hilli sit in the Fire on the Dav of Resurrection.
"Did you hear this from Allah's Messenger (pbuh)?" asked  and M&qal replied, "More than once or twice.
   On the basis of the texts and contents of these foregoing hadiths, scholars have deduced that hoarding is prohibited under two conditions: one, that hoarding at a given time is injurious to the people of that country, and two, that the hoarder's aim is to force the price up in order to make more profit.
Interference in the Free Market
   Another practice related to hoarding which was prohibited by the Prophet (pbuh) is a townsman's selling on behalf of a man from the desert. Scholars have explained the situation in the following manner: a stranger would bring some goods to be sold in town at the current market price. A townsman would approach him, saying, "Leave them with me for a while. I will sell them for you when the price is better." Had the non-resident himself sold his goods, he would have done so for a lower price, thereby benefiting the people, while he himself would have made a reasonable profit.
   This sort of practice was very common in Arab society when Islam came. Anas said, "Sale by a townsman on behalf of a desert-dweller was prohibited to us, even though he might be a blood  From this we learn that for the Muslim the public interest takes precedence over personal relationships. The Prophet (pbuh) said,
"A resident (of town) must not sell for a man from the desert. Leave people alone, so that Allah may give them provision from one another.

l. Narrated by Ahmad and At-Tabarani.
2. by Al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3. Muslim.
   
r
   l'his significant expression of the Prophet's 'Leave people alone, so that Allah may give them provision from one another, " establishes a basic principle in the field of commerce: that the market, its prices, and sales, should be left free to respond to internal economic forces and natural competition without manipulation. When Ibn h Abbas was asked about the meaning of "A resident (Q/ town) must not sell for a man from the desert, " he replied, "The resident should not be a broker for From this we understand that if someone were to inform the man from the desert about prices, offering him good advice and telling him about prevailing market prices without charging him a commission, there would be no harm in it, for giving good advice is part of the religion; in fact, a sound hadith stated,
    "Religion is (the giving ofgood) advice, and,
"(f senneone asks your advice, advise hinr. 
   However, with regard to the broker, it always happens that, in a situation such as that described above, he might neglect the public interest for the sake of his own profit.
Brokerage Is Permissible
   With the exception of such cases, brokerage is permissible, since it is a sort of mediation and connection between the buyer and the seller, which in many cases facilitates a profitable transaction for at least one of them or for both.
   In modern times, middlemen have become more necessary than at any time in the past because of the complexities of trade and conunerce, which involve all types of exports and imports, and wholesale and retail sales and purchases; brokers play a very important role in keeping things moving. There is nothing wrong, therefore, with the broker's charging a commission for his services. The commission may be a fixed amount or proportional to the volume of sales, or whatever is agreed upon among the parties involved.
Al-Bukhari stated in his Sahih,

2. Narrated by Muslim.
3. Narrated by Ahmad.

   Ibn Sirin, N Atal , Ibrahim, and Al-Hasan saw nothing wrong with commissions charged by brokers. Ibn X Abbas said, There is no harm if one person says to another, 'Sell this robe, and if you sell it for more than such and such a price, you may keep the extra amount'. l Ibn Sirin said, 'There is nothing wrong if one person says to another, Sell it for this price and keep the profit, or the profit will be shared between you and me t .
